   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of artificial objects on the Moon
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon_map_grid_showing_artificial_objects_on_moon.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2560" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Moon_map_grid_showing_artificial_objects_on_moon.PNG/220px-Moon_map_grid_showing_artificial_objects_on_moon.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Moon_map_grid_showing_artificial_objects_on_moon.PNG/330px-Moon_map_grid_showing_artificial_objects_on_moon.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Moon_map_grid_showing_artificial_objects_on_moon.PNG/440px-Moon_map_grid_showing_artificial_objects_on_moon.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moon_map_grid_showing_artificial_objects_on_moon.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Locations of large artificial objects on the Moon superimposed on data from the
         <a href="/wiki/Clementine_(spacecraft)" title="Clementine (spacecraft)">
          Clementine (spacecraft)
         </a>
         mission in
         <a href="/wiki/Equirectangular_projection" title="Equirectangular projection">
          equirectangular projection
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       This is a partial listing of artificial materials on the Lunar surface. The table below does not separately list small items such as
       <a href="/wiki/Retroreflector" title="Retroreflector">
        retroreflectors
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Surface_Experiment_Package" title="Apollo Lunar Surface Experiment Package">
        Apollo Lunar Surface Experiment Packages
       </a>
       , or the commemorative, artistic, and personal objects left there by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Apollo" title="Project Apollo">
        Apollo
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronauts" title="Astronauts">
        astronauts
       </a>
       , such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Flag_Assembly" title="Lunar Flag Assembly">
        US flags
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_plaque" title="Lunar plaque">
        commemorative plaques
       </a>
       attached to the ladders of the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module" title="Apollo Lunar Module">
        Apollo Lunar Modules
       </a>
       , the silver
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronaut_pin" title="Astronaut pin">
        astronaut pin
       </a>
       left by
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bean" title="Alan Bean">
        Alan Bean
       </a>
       in honor of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clifton_C._Williams" title="Clifton C. Williams">
        Clifton C. Williams
       </a>
       whom he replaced, the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Fallen_Astronaut" title="Fallen Astronaut">
         Fallen Astronaut
        </a>
       </i>
       statuette and memorial plaque left by the crew of
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">
        Apollo 15
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Golf_ball" title="Golf ball">
        golf balls
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shepard" title="Alan Shepard">
        Alan Shepard
       </a>
       hit during an
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_14" title="Apollo 14">
        Apollo 14
       </a>
       moonwalk.
      </p>
      <p>
       The remains of five
       <a href="/wiki/S-IVB" title="S-IVB">
        S-IVB
       </a>
       third stages of
       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">
        Saturn V
       </a>
       rockets from the Apollo program are the heaviest single pieces sent to the Lunar surface. Humans have left over 187,400 kilograms (413,100 lb) of material on the Moon, and 380 kilograms (838 lb) of
       <a href="/wiki/Moon_rock" title="Moon rock">
        Moon rock
       </a>
       was brought back to Earth by Apollo and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luna_program" title="Luna program">
        Luna
       </a>
       missions. The only artificial objects on the Moon that are still in use are the retroreflectors for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_laser_ranging_experiment" title="Lunar laser ranging experiment">
        lunar laser ranging experiments
       </a>
       left there by the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
        Apollo 11
       </a>
       , 14, and 15 astronauts and by the
       <a href="/wiki/Lunokhod_1" title="Lunokhod 1">
        Lunokhod 1
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lunokhod_2" title="Lunokhod 2">
        Lunokhod 2
       </a>
       missions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Objects at greater than 90 degrees east or west are on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far_side_(Moon)" title="Far side (Moon)">
        far side of the Moon
       </a>
       , including
       <a href="/wiki/Ranger_4" title="Ranger 4">
        Ranger 4
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Orbiter_1" title="Lunar Orbiter 1">
        Lunar Orbiter 1
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Orbiter_2" title="Lunar Orbiter 2">
        Lunar Orbiter 2
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Orbiter_3" title="Lunar Orbiter 3">
        Lunar Orbiter 3
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=NASA+NSSDC+Master+Catalog+-+Apollo+11+LM+descent+stage&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnssdc.gsfc.nasa.gov%2Fnmc%2FspacecraftDisplay.do%3Fid%3D1969-059C&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+artificial+objects+on+the+Moon">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-note2-36">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-note2_36-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-note2_36-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-note2_36-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-note2_36-3">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              d
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-note2_36-4">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              e
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-note2_36-5">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              f
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          The ascent stage of
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_10" title="Apollo 10">
           Apollo 10
          </a>
          was commanded to fire its engine, left lunar orbit and entered solar orbit. The ascent stage of
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
           Apollo 11
          </a>
          was left in orbit and thereafter its orbit decayed and it crashed onto the Moon at an unknown location. The
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_16" title="Apollo 16">
           Apollo 16
          </a>
          ascent stage failed to crash onto moon when commanded and it decayed from orbit at a later date and also crashed at an unknown location. The ascent stages of the remaining successful missions (Apollo
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">
           12
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_14" title="Apollo 14">
           14
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">
           15
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">
           17
          </a>
          ) were each deliberately crashed onto the Moon.
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">
           Apollo 13
          </a>
          's complete
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module" title="Apollo Lunar Module">
           Apollo Lunar Module
          </a>
          re-entered Earth's atmosphere after having served as a lifeboat during the aborted mission.
         </span>
        </li>

             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-note3_40-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luna_program" title="Luna program">
           Luna program
          </a>
          sample return mission; mass listed is for both ascent and descent stages, though only the descent stage was left on the Moon.
         </span>

           The S-IVB/IU impacted the lunar surface at 8:10 p.m. EST on April 14 at a speed of 259 meters per second (incorrect, should probably be 2590 meters/sec), […] 137.1 kilometers from the Apollo 12 seismometer.
